    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer4511377679725353266">Amy Gaer is a busy working wife and mother with young twin boys and a precocious teenage daughter. After returning home from a hectic day at work, Amy greets her children and carves out a few minutes to listen to her daughter sing.   <span id="freeText4511377679725353266" style="display:none">Amy Gaer is a busy working wife and mother with young twin boys and a precocious teenage daughter. After returning home from a hectic day at work, Amy greets her children and carves out a few minutes to listen to her daughter sing. A delicate, silky melody fills the air, and Amy's mind drifts back more than twenty years to a time when everything changed for her…<br /><br />It's 1992. Grunge is on the rise. “Hair bands” are fading. Amy graduates from college and despite a talent for music, she's determined to chase the corporate ladder. Returning to rural Iowa for the summer to live at home with her parents, all her plans shift when Amy meets a local farmer named Nick. A romance blossoms and suddenly the previously banal landscape becomes beautiful. But settling into a life with Nick is far more complicated than she expected, and she is faced with decisions that will alter her life forever.<br /><br />For fans of Emily Giffin and Sophie Kinsella, Goodbye Def Leppard (I'll Miss Those Jeans) is a lighthearted yet poignant tale about life, fate, and the difficult choices we make.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2225246-darcy?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2225246-darcy?shelf=2018">2018</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2181974009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14641234573536050891">The title of this one caught my eye and I put it on my maybe shelf. Finally I decided to dive in and give this one a try. There is so much that I should have liked. I was roughly the same age as the character in the past, I lived in IA, so much was understandable. However I was bored, so very bored. I realized that I didn't care to know what happened to Amy and Nick in the past, if they dated or more. In the end this one wasn't for me.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1729057398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1729057398" />
    <a title="Magpie67" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/987948-magpie67"><img alt="Magpie67" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294634850p2/987948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729057398?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magpie67" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magpie67" href="/user/show/987948-magpie67">Magpie67</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=avoca-book-club">avoca-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=ideas-for-avoca-book-club">ideas-for-avoca-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=september">september</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=met-the-author">met-the-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=2016-titles">2016-titles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=music">music</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/987948-magpie67?shelf=college">college</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729057398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8470253288805696768">"And you may find yourself <br/>Living in a shotgun shack<br/>And you may find yourself <br/>In another part of the world<br/>And you may find yourself <br/>Behind the wheel of a large automobile<br/>And you may find yourself in a beautiful house<br/>With a beautiful wife<br/>And you may ask yourself, well<br/>How did I get here?"<br/><br/>There are days that this song runs through my head as my mantra... Those hectic days where I find myself coming and going with no end in sight. Author Stef Kramer manages to capture the lost feeling a mother of th</span>
  <span id="freeText8470253288805696768" style="display:none">"And you may find yourself <br />Living in a shotgun shack<br />And you may find yourself <br />In another part of the world<br />And you may find yourself <br />Behind the wheel of a large automobile<br />And you may find yourself in a beautiful house<br />With a beautiful wife<br />And you may ask yourself, well<br />How did I get here?"<br /><br />There are days that this song runs through my head as my mantra... Those hectic days where I find myself coming and going with no end in sight. Author Stef Kramer manages to capture the lost feeling a mother of three has one afternoon when Amy's daughter begins to practice her piano and asks for her to listen to the piece. Just the day before Amy's family claimed she was a fun hater as she exploded when she arrived home to a messy kitchen. Yes, the children were making cookies, but as a working mother.... this scene is unsettling some days, some days the mess is too much or is it? <br /><br />"And you may ask yourself<br />How do I work this?<br />And you may ask yourself<br />Where is that large automobile?<br />And you may tell yourself<br />This is not my beautiful house!<br />And you may tell yourself<br />This is not my beautiful wife!"<br /><br />Has anyone wished for one just day to go back to when the days were simple? I have, the smaller apartment, just the dogs, and even... not reporting to a significant other. When the world is collapsing around you and the air is getting thinner... I wish I may, I wish I might, be transformed just one night. What ifs surrounding your soul...<br /><br />So, Amy, a mother of three, working full time with a farmer for a husband... is feeling trapped, antiquated with her daughter's dress code of ripped jeans and possibly unsure of her place in the world, wondering did she make the right decisions at the end of her college years. The music, the beautiful sounds of music, take Amy back to the moment her fork in the road took a turn she was not expecting and this road traveled leads her back to the present. Reflecting on what we need, what we chose, and what could be are often in the back of our minds as the daily grind can get tough. <br /><br />Set in a small town in Iowa with some small town values and farm scenarios. I'm from Omaha and I now live in a small town in Iowa. I related to the book a little different than most, but I found myself taking that trip down memory lane again... wondering... did I take the right fork in the road to follow a small town man back to the roots of a farming community. Reflection and meditation can bring one's perspective back because it's easy to lose it and easy to let go, if one chooses to jump onto another path entirely. Mid-life crisis is what they call that leap of faith. Only the person who waits out the moment and or dives into the next will know how it really turns out. Will you build more character for your future or just leave debris behind?<br /><br />Great first published book for this debut author, High hopes Stef Kramer continues her writing and succeeds beyond her wildest imagination.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8470253288805696768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2385586516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2385586516" />
    <a title="January Gray" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45464723-january-gray"><img alt="January Gray" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576158628p2/45464723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2385586516?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="January Gray" class="user" itemprop="url" name="January Gray" href="/user/show/45464723-january-gray">January Gray</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2385586516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4691409380287209664">I did not love this book, nor did I hate it. I got it because of the title, because I LOVE Def Leppard. (Yes, for that reason.)<br/>This book would make a good Summer/Vacation or "too busy to really read much," type of read, as in that it is interesting, however, you won't miss it if you have to put it down for awhile.<br/>It starts with the main character (Amy) listening to her daughter practice piano, and while doing so, reflects back on her life. It is interesting enough, but then kind of wanders, and </span>
  <span id="freeText4691409380287209664" style="display:none">I did not love this book, nor did I hate it. I got it because of the title, because I LOVE Def Leppard. (Yes, for that reason.)<br />This book would make a good Summer/Vacation or "too busy to really read much," type of read, as in that it is interesting, however, you won't miss it if you have to put it down for awhile.<br />It starts with the main character (Amy) listening to her daughter practice piano, and while doing so, reflects back on her life. It is interesting enough, but then kind of wanders, and sometimes it takes you a minute to realize who is nararating.<br />I think this was intended to be a Girl Meets Boy-loses boy type of book, but I seriously ended up not caring if she and Nick got  together or not.<br />I realize Amy was fresh out of college, but she was 12 year old love struck/forlorn all throughout this book.<br />And, there are several characters in this book who are just there. They really don't have a reason or story line.<br />But never fear, this IS worth reading. As light as it is, I recommend still giving it a read.<br />Amy is one of those types of people who will take the road of least resistance. That is fine, however I was left feeling she was left unhappy with her job choice, and unfortunately took a career path that probably wasn't of her choosing.<br />But...that is the point of this book. Looking back at choices made, re-evaluating your life, and possibly going after your original dream.<br />I could have done without Nick's journal completely.<br />Again, this is a good book to read when you are just looking for something entertaining, but don't expect a deep or complete read.<br />There were a few annoying spelling errors:<br />Head over Heels was written: Head Over Heals<br />And several times, it should have read, "An MBA, not And MBA."<br />This book is getting mixed reviews, and in full-disclosure, most of you know a book like this isn't my particular cup of tea, but I still recommend it. Stick it in your bag for those times you are stuck waiting for the doctor, or want something to read on your lunch break.<br />It's an excellent book to take outside when your kids are playing and you want to read, but still need to give them proper supervision :). You will enjoy this book, but you won't mind when you are interupeted.<br />Here is the link for purchase, and last I checked it is on Kindle Unlimited.<br />I think more people will enjoy it than not.<br />I think the author means for this book to be a stand alone, but I wouldn't mind reading another book of hers telling Nick's side of the story, or continue Amy and Nick's story with him telling it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4691409380287209664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1922899550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922899550" />
    <a title="Kate Vale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14516714-kate-vale"><img alt="Kate Vale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442649894p2/14516714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922899550?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Vale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Vale" href="/user/show/14516714-kate-vale">Kate Vale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14516714-kate-vale?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14516714-kate-vale?shelf=contemp-romance">contemp-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922899550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16318060984113202502">I rarely read autobiographies, but this is a novel that masquerades as one. It begins by asking the question I suspect every woman has asked, probably more than once through her life: how did I get here? Is it where I want to be?<br/><br/>Then, in the course of going back through her memories of her life after she graduates from college and takes a job in banking--hey, did I make a mistake setting aside my music? didn't Mom want me to go to law school?--and thus sets in motion a series of decisions that w</span>
  <span id="freeText16318060984113202502" style="display:none">I rarely read autobiographies, but this is a novel that masquerades as one. It begins by asking the question I suspect every woman has asked, probably more than once through her life: how did I get here? Is it where I want to be?<br /><br />Then, in the course of going back through her memories of her life after she graduates from college and takes a job in banking--hey, did I make a mistake setting aside my music? didn't Mom want me to go to law school?--and thus sets in motion a series of decisions that weren't what she thought she would face. This becomes particularly acute when Amy meets Nick, a not-yet-divorced guy who plays baseball when he's not farming.<br /><br />Set in Iowa and Nebraska, an area of the country I am intimately familiar with, it felt comfortable when the author described the setting. Threading musical references, both classical and rock and pop, throughout the story rendered the female protagonist more real. Aren't we all a combination of disparate sounds and shapes?<br /><br />Finally, we learn that the last pages of the book bring us full circle to where we began this journey--in the present day. This time, however, the questions that plagued the main character (and us?) have been answered. More importantly, they have been accepted. That's what life is: acceptance of the journey that became us.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16318060984113202502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2392282847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2392282847" />
    <a title="No Shelf Control" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77684985-no-shelf-control"><img alt="No Shelf Control" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518444551p2/77684985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2392282847?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="No Shelf Control" class="user" itemprop="url" name="No Shelf Control" href="/user/show/77684985-no-shelf-control">No Shelf Control</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2392282847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1060104540871851305">Present-day mom of three Amy Gaer recounts her experiences back in the early nineties when she was a college student coming home to her parents in rural Iowa where her musician and law school dreams eventually change when she meets dashing farmer Nick. Amy recalls the times she got to meet Nick’s family to how she makes peace with a high school boyfriend of hers to her adventures as a bank teller for a small-town bank in Loam County. Also, Amy’s father calls her Amos probably due to the fact tha</span>
  <span id="freeText1060104540871851305" style="display:none">Present-day mom of three Amy Gaer recounts her experiences back in the early nineties when she was a college student coming home to her parents in rural Iowa where her musician and law school dreams eventually change when she meets dashing farmer Nick. Amy recalls the times she got to meet Nick’s family to how she makes peace with a high school boyfriend of hers to her adventures as a bank teller for a small-town bank in Loam County. Also, Amy’s father calls her Amos probably due to the fact that she is his only child and he wants a son as any typical father would. This does not mean that Mr. Gaer resents her, no, he absolutely loves her. Amy also tells of high school contemporaries of hers who she meets like Shandy Wilson who she describes as her one-time best friend turned nemesis, haha.<br /><br />What I truly liked about this book was that it definitely mirrors my own journey in my adult life. I mean, I could see myself in Amy because we both were English majors in college. I could relate to her love for books and I enjoyed how the author Kramer would have Amy mentioning literary classics like To Kill a Mockingbird, House of Mirth, and East of Eden. I also absolutely loved her way of incorporating rock music into this story where Amy talks about classic rock bands like The Cure, Journey, this book’s namesake Def Leppard, and Motley Crue. I also admire Kramer’s usage of 70’s and 80s song titles like Pink Floyd’s “Another Brick In the Wall”, Eric Clapton’s “Wonderful Tonight”, Madonna’s “Material Girl”, Whitney Houston’s “How Will I Know”, and Blondie’s “Call Me” to name a few. All of those made me really enjoy this book resulting in me reading it in just two days in contrast to my usual reading duration of a week for a book of this book’s length. The most coincidental aspect of this book is how some of Amy’s attributes are similar to mine. In addition to us both being English majors and lovers of music, we also both have something to do with financial institutions. I used to work as a receptionist for a bank in my hometown. It’s such a coincidence it makes me smile.<br /><br />So, who should I recommend this beauty to? I would definitely this book should be read by all college graduates. People who are about to graduate from university and are about to return to their hometowns should give this book a read because it could help them decide on their career paths and goals. I also think that it would be enjoyed by all English majors as well as music majors. I saw myself in Amy and it has made me think about my own future and where I want to be in ten years from now. It’s very real life-like because it’s true that some English majors don’t all end up as writers or teachers. Sometimes we take on careers that are more lucrative because I tell you if you are not savvy about your English degree then you will definitely not make a lot of money with it. So there you have it! I really commend author Stef Kramer for writing this book because it is relatable and definitely describes the reality of having English as your college major. I’m not talking about the negative side of it but the positive aspect of it where you can be anything you want in life if you use your creativity skills that you learned from your college education. Enjoy your day now!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1060104540871851305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2717287075" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2717287075" />
    <a title="Shari Ring Wolf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73500786-shari-ring-wolf"><img alt="Shari Ring Wolf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510017943p2/73500786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2717287075?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shari Ring Wolf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shari Ring Wolf" href="/user/show/73500786-shari-ring-wolf">Shari Ring Wolf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2717287075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15322508853255763026"><strong>Fun read.</strong><br/><br/>Great story. It manages to be thought provoking as well as light, easy, and fun. The characters are likable and believable. The story is structured and paced well, and I loved the way the story was set in present time, recollection, then present time again. The personal cliffhanger kept the reader engaged. Rock songs titled each chapter; I found that nostalgic and cool. I also enjoyed the wit of some of the characters. I do wish it had been edited one more time. <br/>The story’s pace was per</span>
  <span id="freeText15322508853255763026" style="display:none"><strong>Fun read.</strong><br /><br />Great story. It manages to be thought provoking as well as light, easy, and fun. The characters are likable and believable. The story is structured and paced well, and I loved the way the story was set in present time, recollection, then present time again. The personal cliffhanger kept the reader engaged. Rock songs titled each chapter; I found that nostalgic and cool. I also enjoyed the wit of some of the characters. I do wish it had been edited one more time. <br />The story’s pace was perfect, so it was jarring to have to stop and read a sentence several times to figure out what the author meant. Sometimes I had to read aloud: “I would just assume read another chapter in one of my favorite books...” I was trying to figure out what the character was making a small assumption about. I’m guessing she meant, “I would just as soon read another chapter...” There were careless mistakes throughout the book that took away from the reading experience and stopped the pace. Bad editing that takes away from the story felt especially “wrong” in this book because the main character was quite educated. She struggled to be accepting towards the bad grammar of the people in her hometown, and yet it was obvious she couldn’t spell. The errors were more glaring in this book than others I’ve read, because it was such a good story. Talented writing deserves to look professional as well.<br />Overall though, it was a delightful story and I would recommend it to anyone looking for something light but engaging to read. Maybe there will be a rewrite where these errors will be fixed. That would take this book to a 5 star rating for sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15322508853255763026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2410826931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2410826931" />
    <a title="Ebook Boss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82627842-ebook-boss"><img alt="Ebook Boss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527952481p2/82627842.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2410826931?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ebook Boss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ebook Boss" href="/user/show/82627842-ebook-boss">Ebook Boss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2410826931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7396769493046383815">If you are looking for a cracking holiday read, that you can read by the pool in a single afternoon, then look no further than 'Good-Bye Def Leppard' by Stef Kramer. This romantic novel follows Amy Gaer a professional working mother, who flashbacks to her youth and her tumultuous love affair with the recently divorced Nick Klein. Amy is at a pivotal point in her life, completing her final year at university, unsure of what her next step in life will be. Will her new romance make this decision ha</span>
  <span id="freeText7396769493046383815" style="display:none">If you are looking for a cracking holiday read, that you can read by the pool in a single afternoon, then look no further than 'Good-Bye Def Leppard' by Stef Kramer. This romantic novel follows Amy Gaer a professional working mother, who flashbacks to her youth and her tumultuous love affair with the recently divorced Nick Klein. Amy is at a pivotal point in her life, completing her final year at university, unsure of what her next step in life will be. Will her new romance make this decision harder, and will there be room in her future for Nick?<br /><br />In 'Good-Bye Def Leppard' I found a kindred spirit in protagonist Amy. I may not have been a university student in the 1990s, but I definitely empathised with her struggles in the novel and the internal battle that goes on between the head and the heart. I found myself really willing her on throughout the novel, particularly when she experiences some work-place difficulties and discrimination. This novel was very engaging, had a great flow, and was pretty hard to put down – a real triumph for a debut novel.<br /><br />Furthermore, if you are as fond of the music of the 1990s as I am, then you are going to have some pleasant surprises throughout this novel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7396769493046383815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2408666789" />
    <a title="Bookie Wookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82553326-bookie-wookie"><img alt="Bookie Wookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527770613p2/82553326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2408666789?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookie Wookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookie Wookie" href="/user/show/82553326-bookie-wookie">Bookie Wookie</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408666789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10891665914403299128">Amy, our main character here, bumbles through motherhood and an ever-changing society while holding onto the nostalgia of her youth and talent. Moving forward doesn’t have to feel like leaving everything you love and care for behind, and author Stef Kramer navigates this maze quite well through Amy’s recant of her life..<br/><br/>Everything ties together for Amy when she meets someone in the most unexpected of places (per normal for these things). This story is a great journey through the confusion of lif</span>
  <span id="freeText10891665914403299128" style="display:none">Amy, our main character here, bumbles through motherhood and an ever-changing society while holding onto the nostalgia of her youth and talent. Moving forward doesn’t have to feel like leaving everything you love and care for behind, and author Stef Kramer navigates this maze quite well through Amy’s recant of her life..<br /><br />Everything ties together for Amy when she meets someone in the most unexpected of places (per normal for these things). This story is a great journey through the confusion of life, the unexpected bliss of love, and how things tend to shake out just fine in the end (even if it isn’t ideal or what we initially wanted).<br /><br />Stef Kramer’s writing is solid, and though there are many great writers out there, she tells a great piece of fiction that feels biographical.<br /><br />This book is for anyone that questions where they are and how they got here, and for anyone who is looking forward at their path and wondering if things are going to come together. Life is funny in that it tends to work out, and we end up right where we were supposed to be.<br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText3547758841032111831" style="display:none">I'm not usually a big reader of romantic fiction, but how could I turn down a book that has Def Leppard in the title...some of my best memories come from the Def Leppard era, so I was ready for some nostalgia. This is what happens to stressed-out working mum, Amy Gaer when she hears her daughter singing. She begins to reminisce about her life in the early 90s when she was at university an looking towards the future. Then she meets Nick, and everything changes – love can certainly make life complicated. <br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HQfvQoS4Cq+n98OzY6VDGPPjido0lIdubh1gslGZKANICtXPm8wyKwgmNreZbW2MO8Z4sWkzAS/3Wz9ALwSz3g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ffh889E7JH9FAS/qTdZGGec37bZs4AT+Bhwj0V9F+AIo9UZ+zk8c++rQ2u63HmiNLxIc3TFHgr+fWnwjIdhj3w==')})
  }

He escapes to Chicago, only to find himself in a full-scale replica of Ancient Rome in China, erected for the wealthy country’s amusement and manned by a million enslaved Italians. As he struggles to orient himself in these synchronized urban labyrinths, he is plunged back to real Ancient Rome, before being flung yet further into the future: It’s 2115 and the Chinese Empire rules the world. The former Western hemisphere is now the American Special Administrative Region, a vast Cantonese-speaking slave colony. Malmquist will soon be shipped to the most opulent city the world has ever known for an unspeakable fate. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11373085989143438443">Stef Kramer is a writer, blogger, and CFO. She lives on a farm near Earling, Iowa with her husband, two children, and amusing pets. After receiving her Bachelor’s of Arts in English at the University of Iowa, she went on to obtain her MBA at Creighton University. In addition to her two blogs, she is happy to introduce Goodbye Def Leppard (I'll Miss Those Jeans) which was rated as "Outstanding" in </span>
  <span id="freeText11373085989143438443" style="display:none">Stef Kramer is a writer, blogger, and CFO. She lives on a farm near Earling, Iowa with her husband, two children, and amusing pets. After receiving her Bachelor’s of Arts in English at the University of Iowa, she went on to obtain her MBA at Creighton University. In addition to her two blogs, she is happy to introduce Goodbye Def Leppard (I'll Miss Those Jeans) which was rated as "Outstanding" in the Writer's Digest self-published competition and received a positive Kirkus Review. Her short story, "Phoenix Sun" was published by The Story Plant in the anthology entitled Portable Magic. She was named as a runner-up in The Story Plant's Author's First Novels contest.</span>
